[SUCCESS] Result:
The National Wetland Policy of Sri Lanka outlines several key objectives and goals, guided by principles of ecological integrity, sustainable use, community participation, and the precautionary principle [National Wetland Policy, p. 2]. The primary objectives are to conserve and sustainably manage Sri Lanka풉칂칐s wetland resources [National Wetland Policy, p. 3], maintaining ecological integrity and biodiversity, and ensuring the sustainable use of these resources for present and future generations [National Wetland Policy, p. 3]. Specific goals supporting these objectives include increasing the area of protected wetlands by 10% by 2025 and restoring degraded wetland ecosystems to enhance their ecological functions [National Wetland Policy, p. 4].

[SUCCESS] Result:
According to the Metro Colombo Wetland Management Strategy, wetland protection zones are defined as three categories: Core Conservation Zones, Buffer Zones, and Sustainable Use Zones [Metro Colombo Wetland Management Strategy, p. 6]. Core Conservation Zones are areas of high ecological sensitivity with strict protection measures [Metro Colombo Wetland Management Strategy, p. 7]. Buffer Zones provide a transitional area surrounding Core Conservation Zones with regulated activities [Metro Colombo Wetland Management Strategy, p. 7]. Finally, Sustainable Use Zones allow for the sustainable utilization of wetland resources with appropriate management practices [Metro Colombo Wetland Management Strategy, p. 8]. The National Wetland Policy recognizes and supports the Metro Colombo strategy's zoning framework as a model for wetland management across Sri Lanka [National Wetland Policy, p. 11, 12].
